        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165308364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3863619092781701718">Having just finished "Shards of Honor" and "Barrayar", I simply couldn't wait to pick up the first book in the Miles Vorkosigan series. Unfortunately for me, it seems Mrs. Bujold has shifted tones when going from Cordelia to her son Miles.<br/><br/>Where Cordelia's novels were sometimes funny, sometimes inclined to the romantic, but as a whole well-crafted and dramatic, "The Warrior's Apprentice" feels more like a running joke. It seems Mrs. Bujold has decided she would show Miles is human by making him w</span>
  <span id="freeText3863619092781701718" style="display:none">Having just finished "Shards of Honor" and "Barrayar", I simply couldn't wait to pick up the first book in the Miles Vorkosigan series. Unfortunately for me, it seems Mrs. Bujold has shifted tones when going from Cordelia to her son Miles.<br /><br />Where Cordelia's novels were sometimes funny, sometimes inclined to the romantic, but as a whole well-crafted and dramatic, "The Warrior's Apprentice" feels more like a running joke. It seems Mrs. Bujold has decided she would show Miles is human by making him whine, cry, puke his guts out and tremble in fear most of the time, 'in aparté' for the reader. Oh, he also lusts after Elena a lot, and shows us his noble streak by going down the 'unrequited love' path. Bleh.<br /><br />What is particularly irritating about the novel is the way things just fall in place conveniently for Miles. Miles' genius is that which comes forth in second-rate novels, where it is not so much the protagonist that is intelligent, but the rest of the Universe that is downright dumb. Miles recruits people by stuttering half-baked lies; he exposes imperial schemes by confronting admirals with his sharp wit; he outwits entire armies by concocting plans full of assumptions that his enemies conveniently fall into.<br /><br />I realize this novel is intended as light reading, but so were "Shards of Honor" and "Barrayar". They were light reading, filled with drama, action and humor, and a certain dose of romance. "The Warrior's Apprentice" feels like a bad imitation of all that made the Cordelia books so great, and all the characters from these two books are here only as cardboard cutouts reminding us of the clichés at the heart of the vibrant characters we grew to love previously.<br /><br />I wish Miles were more like his mother. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3863619092781701718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_247744744" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/247744744" />
    <a title="Andreea Daia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5267196-andreea-daia"><img alt="Andreea Daia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441815326p2/5267196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/247744744?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreea Daia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreea Daia" href="/user/show/5267196-andreea-daia">Andreea Daia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/12479583-the-warrior-s-apprentice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5267196-andreea-daia?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5267196-andreea-daia?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5267196-andreea-daia?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5267196-andreea-daia?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5267196-andreea-daia?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5267196-andreea-daia?shelf=amazing-characters">amazing-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer247744744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8212434632553458009">I always thought that boys of Miles age (his age as in "The Warrior's Apprentice," that is) are particularly chafing in their self-centeredness, in their self-absorption which prevents them from understanding that their <i>inoffensive</i> acts of "proving themselves" are in actuality harmful to the people they love. Ms. Bujold creates such a believable character that two thirds of the book, I wanted to castigate and point out to him the consequences of his "quest." He is young, consumed by self-doubts </span>
  <span id="freeText8212434632553458009" style="display:none">I always thought that boys of Miles age (his age as in "The Warrior's Apprentice," that is) are particularly chafing in their self-centeredness, in their self-absorption which prevents them from understanding that their <i>inoffensive</i> acts of "proving themselves" are in actuality harmful to the people they love. Ms. Bujold creates such a believable character that two thirds of the book, I wanted to castigate and point out to him the consequences of his "quest." He is young, consumed by self-doubts and lack of identity, frantically searching for a sense of direction, and in his search making mistake after mistake. Ms. Bujold's main character is decidedly <i>real</i>.<br /><br />When I first pondered at the message of this novel and how to write my review, I planned in touching the fact that Miles creates a word in which he belongs, a safe harbor for "broken" people like him, in need of a second chance. But now that I'm writing it, I feel that it's more important to talk about Miles's honor. <br /><br />He starts his journey a virgin, not sexually but integrity wise. His is a fool, but an innocent one, who yet has to break his word. Despite wading in a river of blunders, he somehow succeeds to hold on to that most important principle he inherited from his parents. When he finally understands that doing the right thing means favoring the loved ones' happiness over his own happiness, he is put in the distressing situation of choosing between his word (which at the time he equals with his honor) and the right thing to do. For Miles, failing to keep a promise is a rite of passage, his transition from childhood to manhood, from phantasms to reality. And in his decision, he neither fails nor loses his honor.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[***** Post Scriptum: It is interesting that up to the end Ms. Bujold, through Miles's eyes, seems to believe that he forswears. However, since he bestows the mercenaries (led now by Baz Jesek) upon the Emperor, Elena's husband becomes indeed an imperial officer... Which of course means that Miles both, does the right thing by freeing Elena and keeps his word to Bothari. :)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="8212434632553458009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3151652594" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18252214001853574469">This is the second (by publication order; fourth by internal chronology) volume of Vorkosigan saga. The main character is now the son of Cordelia Naismith and Aral Vorkosigan named Miles. From the previous book we know that during the pregnancy Cordelia was affected by toxin that made Miles bones brittle (and stunted his growth). The book was read a part of Vorkosigan challenge at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/474371-hugo-nebula-awards-best-novels' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hugo & Nebula Awards: Best Novels</a> group.<br/><br/>The story starts as 17-year-old Miles tries to enter the military academy bu</span>
  <span id="freeText18252214001853574469" style="display:none">This is the second (by publication order; fourth by internal chronology) volume of Vorkosigan saga. The main character is now the son of Cordelia Naismith and Aral Vorkosigan named Miles. From the previous book we know that during the pregnancy Cordelia was affected by toxin that made Miles bones brittle (and stunted his growth). The book was read a part of Vorkosigan challenge at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/474371-hugo-nebula-awards-best-novels" rel="nofollow noopener">Hugo &amp; Nebula Awards: Best Novels</a> group.<br /><br />The story starts as 17-year-old Miles tries to enter the military academy but (predictably) fails at physical. As a conciliation prize, he with Bothari and his daughter Helen visit Cordelia’s mother on Beta Colony. Here Mile almost immediately stumbles into a conflict that he resolves by buying a space freighter to help a total stranger.<br /><br />The book’s start is filled with Chekhov’s guns: Miles and Helen are hoping to find Helen’s mother and decipher why Bothari’s service records are classified and (what a surprise!) they travel to Beta, where we, the readers, know her mother should be; Miles goes in debt to buy an obsolete freighter – of course he will use it sooner or later! At the same time, while we understand that these guns will shoot, just how and why will nevertheless be a surprise.<br /><br />The series effect on me is quite bizarre. It seems so simple and almost juvenile, but like the best works of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/205.Robert_A__Heinlein" title="Robert A. Heinlein" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert A. Heinlein</a> it drives you on to read more and more. And the themes it raises are simple only on a first glance. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16094.Lois_McMaster_Bujold" title="Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Lois McMaster Bujold</a> is truly a great master!<br /></span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9404426360214663648"><i>“Huh. Didn’t they give you any medical treatment?” <br/>"Oh, sure. I’ve had an Inquisition’s worth. That’s why I can walk around today, instead of being carried in a bucket.”</i><br/><br/>After meeting baby Miles at the end of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2176052251?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Barrayar</a>, I finally got to know the main protagonist of the Vorkosigan Saga.<br/><br/>Part of buddy reading the series with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads' rel='nofollow noopener'>SpecFic</a> in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/98254-vorkosigan-saga-chronological' rel='nofollow noopener'>chronological order</a>.<br/><br/>This book didn't pull its punches and got right into the middle of the action.   <span id="freeText9404426360214663648" style="display:none"><i>“Huh. Didn’t they give you any medical treatment?” <br />"Oh, sure. I’ve had an Inquisition’s worth. That’s why I can walk around today, instead of being carried in a bucket.”</i><br /><br />After meeting baby Miles at the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2176052251?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Barrayar</a>, I finally got to know the main protagonist of the Vorkosigan Saga.<br /><br />Part of buddy reading the series with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">SpecFic</a> in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/98254-vorkosigan-saga-chronological" rel="nofollow noopener">chronological order</a>.<br /><br />This book didn't pull its punches and got right into the middle of the action. Still, I felt no great need to keep going and it took me a week to just get past the first third of the book. Seems to be a pattern for me with this series. The beginning seemingly drags a lot and about 30 to 40% it gets more interesting. I just wish these books would pick up speed a little faster. I know, I am contradicting myself. Maybe it's the narrative of the series in general that doesn't hold my attention? Although, I have to admit that it is quite funny to read about Miles digging the hole he is standing in deeper and deeper...<br /><br />I was entertained, I laughed, but I also skimmed. Nice plot, but also not really doing it for me. I don't know, I guess I will have to read another one!<br /><br />3.25 undecided stars...</span>

<div id="review_3153171144" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3153171144" />
    <a title="Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10818276-lee"><img alt="Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341872613p2/10818276.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3153171144?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/10818276-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6057779-the-warrior-s-apprentice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=netgalleyreaders2020">netgalleyreaders2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=vorkosigan-series-challenge">vorkosigan-series-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=war">war</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3153171144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11375765498011311509">The Warrior’s Apprentice introduces Miles Vorkosigan as the ongoing lead protagonist of this book series, following on from his parents who were the leads in the previous two books. A lot of people say you can start the saga with this book but I would definitely recommend reading Shards of Honour and Barrayar first. I think you’d definitely be confused by quite a few aspects of Warrior’s Apprentice if you hadn’t bothered.<br/><br/>The beginning of the book is fantastic. 17 year-old Miles desperately wants</span>
  <span id="freeText11375765498011311509" style="display:none">The Warrior’s Apprentice introduces Miles Vorkosigan as the ongoing lead protagonist of this book series, following on from his parents who were the leads in the previous two books. A lot of people say you can start the saga with this book but I would definitely recommend reading Shards of Honour and Barrayar first. I think you’d definitely be confused by quite a few aspects of Warrior’s Apprentice if you hadn’t bothered.<br /><br />The beginning of the book is fantastic. 17 year-old Miles desperately wants to live up to his Vor heritage and become part of the military. Unfortunately, his brittle bones and impairments (caused by an assassination attempt when he was in vitro), means he fails the physical tests required. I loved this part. My heart just broke at Miles’s [obviously mistaken] belief that his parents and grandfather think he’s a disappointment.<br /><br />The middle part of the books has Miles travelling to his mother’s planet of Beta where his initial plan is to find the truth about his childhood friend (and unrequited love) Elena Bothari’s mother. The background of Elena’s parentage was explained in Shards of Honor and Barrayar and this is another reason why I think you need to read those two books first. I guess LMB explains things, in a manner, but there’s a lot of implying the reader already knows the devastating truth.<br /><br />Along the way, Miles somehow finds himself the leader of a band of mercenaries and involved in an interplanetary war, weapons smuggling, and a payroll heist. Unfortunately, this part of the book dragged for me a bit. I know it was supposed to show how charismatic, intelligent and empathetic Miles is despite his handicaps but, at times, it became confusing and a little young adult for my liking. (Confusing as in, there seemed to be too many characters and political situations I needed to follow.) I much preferred the book once its setting returned to Barrayar.<br /><br />Miles’s life as a mercenary of course, highlights that even though Miles thinks otherwise due to his physical issues, the apple doesn’t fall far from the tree and he’s perfectly suited as a military strategist.<br /><br />I wasn’t a huge fan of Elena’s. She is so overtly feminist that, at times, it felt like it was just too much, if you know what I mean. I much preferred Cordelia’s more subtle feminism.<br /><br />Unlike most other reviewers of this series, I can’t say I hated Ivan, Miles’s cousin. Okay, he’s dumb but he still was fiercely loyal to Aral and Miles which I appreciated.<br /><br />Elena Bothari’s father redeemed himself to me in this installment. There was a lot about him in the previous two books that made me uncomfortable but his paternal protectiveness with both Miles and Elena made me realise he was at least trying to right wrongs from the past. The love Miles gives him in return definitely made me tear up.<br /><br />Actually, the recurring theme of parental love was my favourite thing about this book. Miles’s complicated relationship with his father, and Aral and Cordelia’s equally complicated one with his grandfather, to me were the heart, and heartbreaking best moments, of the story. There are even pseudo paternal moments between Aral and Emperor Gregor that were heartbreakingly sad. (I love Aral so much and adored every scene he was featured in and every time Miles tried to emulate him. *sigh*)<br /><br />Again, LMB wrote this in 1986 and you’d expect a lot of the scifi aspects to be dated but again, LMB does extremely well. Not that I think the scifi gadget/weapons/battles are the important part of these books. It’s all about the characters and LMB’s penchant for dialogue heavy scenes always supports this theory.<br /><br />Anyway, I guess in the grand scheme of things, I didn’t love this book as much as its two predecessors but it is still a nice introduction to Miles. I definitely instantly loved him and can’t wait to read the journey LMB takes him on.<br /><br />4 ½ out of 5</span>
  <a data-text-id="11375765498011311509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2474937956" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2474937956" />
    <a title="aPriL does feral sometimes " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes"><img alt="aPriL does feral sometimes " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478243665p2/3409532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2474937956?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="aPriL does feral sometimes " class="user" itemprop="url" name="aPriL does feral sometimes " href="/user/show/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes">aPriL does feral sometimes </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12779132-the-warrior-s-apprentice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=awesomely-silly-but-i-loved-it">awesomely-silly-but-i-loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=a-jack-in-the-box-pop-surprise">a-jack-in-the-box-pop-surprise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=cheap-thrills-but-i-loved-it">cheap-thrills-but-i-loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=meaningless-cover-art">meaningless-cover-art</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2474937956" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17195658126654286685"><strong>Wonderfully fun!</strong><br/><br/>‘The Warrior’s Apprentice’ is book two in the Vorkosigan Saga by publishing date, but I think it is actually book three, following the two books <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/531792.Shards_of_Honor__Vorkosigan_Saga__1_' title='Shards of Honor (Vorkosigan Saga #1) by Lois McMaster Bujold' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shards of Honor</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61905.Barrayar__Vorkosigan_Saga___7_' title='Barrayar (Vorkosigan Saga, #7) by Lois McMaster Bujold' rel='nofollow noopener'>Barrayar</a> chronologically in time. ‘Shards of Honor’ and ‘Barrayar’ show how the character Miles Vorkosian’s parents meet, and why Miles has a deformed body. The rest of the series after these two books follow Miles primarily in his adventures. <br/><br/>Miles clearly is a rascal character similar to Hans Solo of the Star Wars m</span>
  <span id="freeText17195658126654286685" style="display:none"><strong>Wonderfully fun!</strong><br /><br />‘The Warrior’s Apprentice’ is book two in the Vorkosigan Saga by publishing date, but I think it is actually book three, following the two books <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/531792.Shards_of_Honor__Vorkosigan_Saga__1_" title="Shards of Honor (Vorkosigan Saga #1) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Shards of Honor</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61905.Barrayar__Vorkosigan_Saga___7_" title="Barrayar (Vorkosigan Saga, #7) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Barrayar</a> chronologically in time. ‘Shards of Honor’ and ‘Barrayar’ show how the character Miles Vorkosian’s parents meet, and why Miles has a deformed body. The rest of the series after these two books follow Miles primarily in his adventures. <br /><br />Miles clearly is a rascal character similar to Hans Solo of the Star Wars movies, unlike his noble parents, Cordelia Naismith and Aral Vorkosigan. Aral is a high-ranking aristocrat of the planet Barrayar, and he, almost, completely embraces the honor mores of his planet, which appear to be modeled on an 19th-century version of Russia, only with spacecraft and laser guns. Cordelia comes from a liberal planet and a more technologically advanced world, Beta Colony, which, for instance, forces all criminals into intensive mind-remolding psychotherapy rather than prison. It is a debatable which is a worse sentence, but there is no death sentence on Beta, unlike Barrayar where the sentence of hanging for crimes is one of their mildest death sentences.<br /><br />Miles is seventeen years old. His life seems to be heading for one of incredible boredom as a son of an elite aristocratic Barrayaran family. He failed in his quest to become an officer in the Barrayaran Imperial Military Service, to his enormous grief, because of his weak bones. Plus, his unrequited love for Elena Bothari looks to never be requited. Most Barrayaran men see Miles as someone who should have been exposed to the elements and killed as a newborn, a common occurrence on Barrayar, because of his physical deformities, so most turn their backs on him when it normally is time he join their political parties. Miles is actually a genius, not that anyone on Barrayar cares except for his parents.<br /><br />Miles is at loose ends, so his parents suggest he visit his grandmother on Beta Colony. As this also happens to coincide with Elena’s new curiosity about her mother whose grave may be on Beta Colony or on the planet Escobar, they both go. His parents are relieved. No way could their too intelligent and precocious son get into trouble in such a tame environment as Beta Colony, right? Right?<br /><br />I was laughing and commiserating very quickly with Miles from the beginning of the book. From the first chapter to the last, Lois McMaster Bujold never lets up on the action and surprises in this comedy-drama series. I never lost interest in this book, and the author never missteps in her writing or plotting. It is very much an atmosphere which reminded me of the Marx Brothers movies. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marx_Brothers">https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marx_...</a><br /><br />Bujold is such a GREAT author. She creates fantastic yet plausible worlds in every series she has created, with dramatic atmospheres of suitable seriousness, drama and comedy, depending on the series or character. I highly recommend ALL of her novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17195658126654286685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_644891708" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/644891708" />
    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/644891708?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanda" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda">Wanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780671655877" href="/book/show/531793.The_Warrior_s_Apprentice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=reading-project">reading-project</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=military-science-fiction">military-science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=used-books">used-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=female-authors">female-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer644891708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11423869515932636421"><b>A rolling stone gathers no moss.</b> Miles Naismith Vorkosigan, with his favourite saying at the ending of the book being “Forward momentum,” will never grow any moss. At the end of <i>Barrayar</i>, Miles is a small, brittle-boned child with a reluctance to sit still and preternatural speed for finding the next predicament to get into. He is able to keep three or four adults hopping and still regularly break his bones while performing these antics.<br/><br/><i>The Warrior’s Apprentice</i> introduces the reader to Miles, th</span>
  <span id="freeText11423869515932636421" style="display:none"><b>A rolling stone gathers no moss.</b> Miles Naismith Vorkosigan, with his favourite saying at the ending of the book being “Forward momentum,” will never grow any moss. At the end of <i>Barrayar</i>, Miles is a small, brittle-boned child with a reluctance to sit still and preternatural speed for finding the next predicament to get into. He is able to keep three or four adults hopping and still regularly break his bones while performing these antics.<br /><br /><i>The Warrior’s Apprentice</i> introduces the reader to Miles, the young man. Still determined, still looking to make his mark in the world, but rapidly washing out of Barrayaran military school due to his physical limitations. So what will he do with his life once the military life is ruled out? It becomes expedient for Miles to visit his maternal grandmother in Beta Colony and the adventure begins.<br /><br />Miles is a perfect balance of his genetics—he has his father’s mind for strategy and politics and his mother’s Betan heart for people, understanding them and wanting to help. The combination launches him on his big adventure almost by accident. His grandmother Naismith acknowledges his propensity to “pick up strays” and with his first two acts of kindness he attracts his first two devoted followers. <br /><br />One thing leads to another and soon Miles is an accidental military leader and leaning on what he has learned by spending time with his father plus what he can steal time to study on the job. Fake it till you make it. <br /><br />A rollicking adventure with a satisfying ending. No cliff-hanger, but obviously set up for the further adventures of Miles Vorkosigan, which I look forward to reading.<br /><br />Book number 214 in my science fiction and fantasy reading project.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11423869515932636421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_380136067" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/380136067" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4086118-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567611029p2/4086118.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/380136067?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/4086118-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780671720667" href="/book/show/296139.The_Warrior_s_Apprentice">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=military">military</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer380136067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10803890676141186532">A total delight. A space opera full of comedy while wrapped around tragedy, a social satire, and a coming of age tale. Though third in the Vorkosigan series, it is the first in the series with Miles Vorkosigan as the star. Son of a plantetary Prime Minister, Miles at 17 gets booted out of the Imperial Academy due to limitations of a birth defect affecting his legs and soon finds a secret pathway to fulfill his ambitions for accomplishments while on an interstellar excursion. From a small act of </span>
  <span id="freeText10803890676141186532" style="display:none">A total delight. A space opera full of comedy while wrapped around tragedy, a social satire, and a coming of age tale. Though third in the Vorkosigan series, it is the first in the series with Miles Vorkosigan as the star. Son of a plantetary Prime Minister, Miles at 17 gets booted out of the Imperial Academy due to limitations of a birth defect affecting his legs and soon finds a secret pathway to fulfill his ambitions for accomplishments while on an interstellar excursion. From a small act of kindness in helping a washed-up pilot in an arms shipping scheme, he ends up in the middle of a planetary civil war. With each improvisation in problem solving, his schemes escalate, and he ends up "accidentally" building up a mercenary space navy. His ability to empower and empathize with others was modeled on Bujold's understanding of Lawrence of Arabia, while his internal insecurities make him a character anyone could identify with. If like me, you have dabbled in some of the more current chapters in the saga, it is definitely worth going back to the beginning. This 1986 novel was included in "Young Miles", a collection of novels and novellas bringing him into his 20s.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10803890676141186532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_284597747" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/284597747" />
    <a title="John Carter McKnight" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2410586-john-carter-mcknight"><img alt="John Carter McKnight" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380249466p2/2410586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/284597747?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Carter McKnight" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Carter McKnight" href="/user/show/2410586-john-carter-mcknight">John Carter McKnight</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer284597747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11598143139939648128">You can't step in the same river twice, and this SF coming-of-age novel reads very differently in my 40s than it did in my 20s. Frankly, it's even better now than the beloved treasure it used to be. The Warrior's Apprentice is a comedy in the Shakespearian sense: while frequently laugh-till-you hurt hilarious, it's a rich study of character and culture.<br/><br/>Shakespeare would've loved young Miles, who's a goodhearted Richard III, if one can imagine, an off-the-leash lunatic with a gift for persuasion,</span>
  <span id="freeText11598143139939648128" style="display:none">You can't step in the same river twice, and this SF coming-of-age novel reads very differently in my 40s than it did in my 20s. Frankly, it's even better now than the beloved treasure it used to be. The Warrior's Apprentice is a comedy in the Shakespearian sense: while frequently laugh-till-you hurt hilarious, it's a rich study of character and culture.<br /><br />Shakespeare would've loved young Miles, who's a goodhearted Richard III, if one can imagine, an off-the-leash lunatic with a gift for persuasion, who ends up in far over his head. Miles, broken in body, if not quite in spirit, has a gift for drawing to himself the broken and hopeless and bringing out the greatness in them, and in himself... at a cost. <br /><br />Bujold's Miles Vorkosigyn novels are perhaps the best character studies, the best-constructed comedies and dramas, in contemporary literature, genre or otherwise. And they've aged very, very well. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11598143139939648128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('puk9mdIjHYClRyNoimWGdmDPIlBUTBcNmrXQO5W6sHGcz1RLaX3U6AJslwl9kIyptpDFmJrBmWrBy5aKWPlC6w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9dZbeGSI0tQrydTeoGL4pBj7XWSD932q7JxFOaJxUdfP8DKq39YbvIziYL9Xl/J7zqS6rE1688234gOIbzKjTQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer655545220657413685">Lois McMaster Bujold was born in 1949, the daughter of an engineering professor at Ohio State University, from whom she picked up her early interest in science fiction. She now lives in Minneapolis, and has two grown children. <br/><br/>Her fantasy from HarperCollins includes the award-winning Chalion series and the Sharing Knife tetralogy; her science fiction from Baen Books features the perennially bestse</span>
  <span id="freeText655545220657413685" style="display:none">Lois McMaster Bujold was born in 1949, the daughter of an engineering professor at Ohio State University, from whom she picked up her early interest in science fiction. She now lives in Minneapolis, and has two grown children. <br /><br />Her fantasy from HarperCollins includes the award-winning Chalion series and the Sharing Knife tetralogy; her science fiction from Baen Books features the perennially bestselling Vorkosigan Saga. Her work has been translated into over twenty languages.<br /><br />A listing of her awards and nominations may be seen here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.sfadb.com/Lois_McMaster_Bujold">http://www.sfadb.com/Lois_McMaster_Bu...</a><br /> <br />A listing of her interviews is here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://vorkosigan.wikia.com/wiki/Author_Interviews">http://vorkosigan.wikia.com/wiki/Auth...</a><br /><br />An older fan-run site devoted to her work, The Bujold Nexus, is here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.dendarii.com/">http://www.dendarii.com/</a><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="655545220657413685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

The choice is not a popular one on Komarr, where a betrayal a generation before drenched the name of Vorkosigan in blood. Thus, the Komarrans surrounding Miles could be loyal subjects, potential hostages, innocent victims, or rebels ready for revenge. Lies within lies, treachery within treachery, Miles is caught in a race against time to stop a plot that could exile him from Barrayar forever. His burning hope lies in an unexpected ally, one with wounds as deep and honor as beleaguered as his own.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"9903421983798173709\" href=\"#\" This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
